#

#
# -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Ion codes
#
# The following codes use the PDG-2006 conventions.
# The (hyper)nuclear codes are given as a 10-digit number: 10LZZZAAAI where
#   - AAA is the total baryon number,
#   - ZZZ is the total charge,
#   - L is the number of strange quarks,
#   - I is the isomer number (I=0 corresponds to the ground state)
# See the Particle Data book for more details
# -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#
# Feb 2016  updated using latest 2012 official isotope masses.
# Equivalently from either
# http://amdc.impcas.ac.cn/evaluation/data2012/data/mass.mas12
# or
# http://www.nist.gov/pml/data/comp.cfm
#
# cite The relative atomic masses of the isotopes data were published by
# M. Wang, G. Audi, A.H. Wapstra, F.G. Kondev, M. MacCormick, X. Xu1,
# and B. Pfeiffer inThe AME2012 Atomic Mass Evaluation.
# Chinese Physics C 36 (2012) 1287-1602
#
# Then converted from atomic mass in u to nucleus mass in GeV
# multiply by 0.931494095 GeV/c^2/amu
# and subtract Z x 0.000510998910 GeV
#
#----- remnant additions for MEC removal of two nucleons
#
# These use double the mass of the proton and neutron earlier (which are off in last digit from pdg now)
  999 n+n-remnant   1000000020 0 100 PseudoIon  0 1.87914   0.00000e+00 -100 -1 -100 -1   -1   0
#         1     0   1.00000E+00   2     2112     2112                                     neutron    neutron
  999 p+p-remnant   1000020020 0 100 PseudoIon  6 1.87654   0.00000e+00 -100 -1 -100 -1   -1   0
#         1     0   1.00000E+00   2     2212     2212                                     proton     proton
# n+p leftover should really be distinguished from H2 somehow
#  999 n+p-remnant   1000010020 0 100 PseudoIon  3 1.87784   0.00000e+00 -100 -1 -100 -1   -1   1
#        1     0   1.00000E+00   2     2112     2212                                     neutron    proton
